  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ad154742-478d-4286-bc78-2e06fed63cae'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText15461596820725639333" style="display:none">Fresh from a brief stay at a psych hospital, reporter Camille Preaker faces a troubling assignment: she must return to her tiny hometown to cover the unsolved murder of a preteen girl and the disappearance of another. For years, Camille has hardly spoken to her neurotic, hypochondriac mother or to the half-sister she barely knows: a beautiful thirteen-year-old with an eerie grip on the town. Now, installed in her old bedroom in her family's Victorian mansion, Camille finds herself identifying with the young victims—a bit too strongly. Dogged by her own demons, she must unravel the psychological puzzle of her own past if she wants to get the story—and survive this homecoming.<br /><br /><i>Librarian's Note: this is an alternate cover edition - ISBN 10: 0307341550 (ISBN 13: 9780307341556)</i></span>

<div id="review_358300853" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/358300853" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/358300853?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780297851530" href="/book/show/303774.Sharp_Objects">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Emily May by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358300853" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16373467302000791690"><blockquote>
  <i>“The face you give the world tells the world how to treat you.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>There is something deeply unhealthy about this book</b>. It's in the characters, in the story, in the relationships, in the sex, and just in the general mood of the novel. Reading this made me feel a little unwell, both physically and mentally, but I am glad I did. If you know me, you'll know I love complex characters with issues that feel raw and real, rather than melodramatic. The people in this novel are majorly fucked up, no one </span>
  <span id="freeText16373467302000791690" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“The face you give the world tells the world how to treat you.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>There is something deeply unhealthy about this book</b>. It's in the characters, in the story, in the relationships, in the sex, and just in the general mood of the novel. Reading this made me feel a little unwell, both physically and mentally, but I am glad I did. If you know me, you'll know I love complex characters with issues that feel raw and real, rather than melodramatic. The people in this novel are majorly fucked up, no one is without a dark past and everyone, it seems, has a horror story.<br /><br />The protagonist - Camille Preaker - was just thirteen when her sister died and fuelled by grief (amongst other things) Camille spent her teen years carving words into her flesh, covering almost every inch of her body with the marks of her pain. Ten years later, Camille Preaker is now a journalist who returns to the small town of her youth to report on the murders of two young girls - girls who had had all of their teeth removed.<br /><br />Camille is soon caught up in the town once again, she tries to get along with the mother who never loved her and establish a relationship with the troublesome half sister she hardly knows. It seems that once again <b>small towns hold the biggest secrets</b> and Camille finds herself getting dragged deeper and deeper into the investigation, her fragile state of mind constantly threatening to tip her over the edge.<br /><br />This is one mean and nasty book. I knew I was getting a dark, psychological thriller, but I expected something on par with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/237209.In_the_Woods__Dublin_Murder_Squad___1_" title="In the Woods (Dublin Murder Squad, #1) by Tana French" rel="nofollow noopener">In The Woods</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/138825.Tana_French" title="Tana French" rel="nofollow noopener">Tana French</a>. Um, not exactly. Flynn never shies away from the horrific details. You're not going to find anything pleasant in this story; sex, for example, is always something complex - it's an escape or a bargain or a catharsis. Everything else is similar.<br /><br />Flynn does a fantastic job of challenging the notion that women are weak, innocent, damsels in distress. In a world where women are victims - both in their media representation and in statistics - this is a very interesting look at other kinds of women. It's programmed into us to believe that women are safer, kinder, built with an instinct that makes it difficult for them to be cruel and cause pain without reason. <b>Maybe we were always wrong.</b><br /><br />Last updated: April 2016<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16373467302000791690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_385291861" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/385291861" />
    <a title="RandomAnthony" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/721021-randomanthony"><img alt="RandomAnthony" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470919631p2/721021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/385291861?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RandomAnthony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RandomAnthony" href="/user/show/721021-randomanthony">RandomAnthony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780307341549" href="/book/show/66559.Sharp_Objects">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer385291861" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8425239931413414385">Last week I read the fuck out of Gillian Flynn's catalog. Three novels in eight days while my wife and kids were out of town and a sweltering late July marooned me in one of the house's two air conditioned rooms. So although this review is primarily for <i>Sharp Objects</i>, my favorite of Flynn's trio, let me go on record with <i>Gone Girl</i> (four stars, go read another of the zillion of reviews) and <i>Dark Places</i> (three stars, maybe too many narratives perspectives and too willing to wallow in the muck) as </span>
  <span id="freeText8425239931413414385" style="display:none">Last week I read the fuck out of Gillian Flynn's catalog. Three novels in eight days while my wife and kids were out of town and a sweltering late July marooned me in one of the house's two air conditioned rooms. So although this review is primarily for <i>Sharp Objects</i>, my favorite of Flynn's trio, let me go on record with <i>Gone Girl</i> (four stars, go read another of the zillion of reviews) and <i>Dark Places</i> (three stars, maybe too many narratives perspectives and too willing to wallow in the muck) as well, but I'm not writing reviews for those two. <i>Sharp Objects</i>, to me, stands out as Flynn's best so far. The narrator and the storyline don't dance with each other in a seamless, synchronized manner; family history and unwritten community norms mosh-pit it up until the collective response to the murders reminded me of that Soundgarden video where all the faces go funhouse-mirror-y. This narrator isn't a shining heroine. She's very human, supremely fucked up, trying to make sense and move forward. Maybe that's what makes <i>Sharp Objects</i> so interesting. <br /><br />Highly recommended, <i>Sharp Objects</i> is the kind of book one could characterize as a summer read. This is the rare novel that both devoted and casual (yes, that sound you hear is me turning up my nose) readers will appreciate, as long as they can handle the psychological darkness. Good for any season, not just a summer read, even. My nose just turned up a little higher. I better stop now before I'm looking at the ceiling.<br /><br />(By the way, if I haven't said so yet, Gillian Flynn is knee-weakening cute.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8425239931413414385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_28968665" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/28968665" />
    <a title="Simon Cleveland, PhD" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1127870-simon-cleveland-phd"><img alt="Simon Cleveland, PhD" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442439498p2/1127870.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/28968665?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simon Cleveland, PhD" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simon Cleveland, PhD" href="/user/show/1127870-simon-cleveland-phd">Simon Cleveland, PhD</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780307341549" href="/book/show/66559.Sharp_Objects">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28968665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2488835599875195383">The razor blade on the front cover of the book is what one yearns for right after embarking on this read, sharp blade with which to cut every single page, one by one, until they are so neatly shredded that even the memory of what was written on them becomes non existent. And then, one can use the same razor to end one's own life. <br/><br/>I'm still unsure what the author was thinking when she began this book, unless she had some very deep and very disturbing mental issues to work through. <br/><br/>This book is da</span>
  <span id="freeText2488835599875195383" style="display:none">The razor blade on the front cover of the book is what one yearns for right after embarking on this read, sharp blade with which to cut every single page, one by one, until they are so neatly shredded that even the memory of what was written on them becomes non existent. And then, one can use the same razor to end one's own life. <br /><br />I'm still unsure what the author was thinking when she began this book, unless she had some very deep and very disturbing mental issues to work through. <br /><br />This book is dangerous and not because it excites one with a thrilling and suspenseful story. It is dangerous because once one reads it, one loses any desire to look for another book that may restore one's faith in the existence of good books with an uplifting charge. Not only is this book dangerous, but it is sick. Its underlying sickness is that it's emotionally draining and unless readers are looking to load up on more mental baggage (I can't think of anyone who doesn't have enough), I'd stay away from its pain. <br /><br />The main character is a female reporter who returns home on an assignment (covering the serial murders of two little girls). As memories of her painful childhood emerge, readers find a lot more about her character, for example her alcoholic addiction and her obsession to carve words into her own flesh. Waves of her unresolved issues wash away further hopes of a challenging literary work as readers are practically dragged into her problems (not loved enough by her mother, not popular enough in school, not motivated enough in her work) and are subjected to the anguish of either feeling sorry for her or wanting to end her existence. <br /><br />As disturbing details of the two murders resurface, readers are introduced to yet two more characters as equally unpleasant as the first. There is the psychologically unstable (almost emotionally poisonous) personality of her mother and the pathologically sinister and equally disturbed one of the teenage sister. And of course there are the endlessly problematic and mentally crushing details of the small-town's Midwest America (why would one want to read this is beyond my understanding). <br /><br />This book robs one of smiles, of the beauty of life, and even of the reason for love. It is not only bitter, but leaves one with an unpleasant smell of what I'd like to call rotten feelings. I can't brand the book dull (as it did leave me with unwanted thoughts), but I can promise you that you'll feel dull once you've read it. I don't recommend it, but may compare the feelings I have for it to what Chuck Palahniuk's 'Choke' birthed in me.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2488835599875195383" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2822771265627929454"><b>Little buddy read with Her Majesty <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/11644154-la-lionne' rel='nofollow noopener'>La Lionne</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/11731184-9-3-4' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jerry</a> on January 31st!! :D</b><br/><br/>This is my third <b>Gillian Flynn</b> book, after <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8442457.Gone_Girl' title='Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gone Girl</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5886881.Dark_Places' title='Dark Places by Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dark Places</a>. The first one blew my mind, the second one freaked me out a little and this one really scared me. <br/><br/>Sure, after reading 5% of it I was like <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383461624ra/6568783.gif' alt='Hosted by imgur.com' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>--a creepy story with the potential of giving me special nightmares, <br/><br/>but by 90% I was like<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380231251ra/681278.gif' alt='Hosted by imgur.com' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>WTF did I just read??<br/><br/>All the characters were disturbing, <s>especially</s> even the children. <br/><br/>Allow me to start with <b>Camille</b>. She's a </span>
  <span id="freeText2822771265627929454" style="display:none"><b>Little buddy read with Her Majesty <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/11644154-la-lionne" rel="nofollow noopener">La Lionne</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/11731184-9-3-4" rel="nofollow noopener">Jerry</a> on January 31st!! :D</b><br><br>This is my third <b>Gillian Flynn</b> book, after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8442457.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5886881.Dark_Places" title="Dark Places by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Places</a>. The first one blew my mind, the second one freaked me out a little and this one really scared me. <br><br>Sure, after reading 5% of it I was like <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383461624ra/6568783.gif" alt="Hosted by imgur.com" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>--a creepy story with the potential of giving me special nightmares, <br><br>but by 90% I was like<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380231251ra/681278.gif" alt="Hosted by imgur.com" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>WTF did I just read??<br><br>All the characters were disturbing, <s>especially</s> even the children. <br><br>Allow me to start with <b>Camille</b>. She's a reporter, a writer. She's practically obsessed with words, even if they are scribbled on her skin<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380231251i/681279.jpg" alt="Hosted by imgur.com" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>and not necessarily with a pen or marker, if you get my drift. She's a little better now, but you never know what can make her snap and get back to her old habit.<br><br>I can't say I liked her. I hated the way she <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[used Richard and John, her lack of reason, her irresponsibility when she took X with Amma, her 13 year-old half-sister <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Yes, Camille, I get that you're fucked-up, but you're 30, get a grip or see a therapist!<br><br><b>Amma</b>, Camille's 13 year-old half-sister, is a piece of work.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380231251i/681280.jpg" alt="Hosted by imgur.com" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It sure would, sweetie, it sure would...<br><br>I hated her with a vengeance for countless reasons, but most importantly because she was a little bitch, in all the senses of the word. <br><br><b>Adora</b>, the matriarch of the family, Camille and Amma's mother, was also a vision to behold: a bad mother suffering from <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Münchausen syndrome <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, who felt the need to bring another child into the world, after Marian, only to smother her in torture and drive her to madness and eventually <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[murder. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Who's left? The only character I remotely liked was <b>Richard</b>, the cop. He was hot. He would have been so good for Camille. But noooo, she just had to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ruin it all by becoming a cradle-robber under the convenient pretext that she felt the need to comfort and be comforted <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380231251ra/681281.gif" alt="Hosted by imgur.com" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As much as the characters annoyed and disturbed me, I enjoyed the story very much. It was shocking, unexpected, creepy, not funny at all and extremely well-written. I will definitely be reading more of <b>Gillian Flynn's</b> novels!<br><br><b>5 stars!!</b> <br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2365419705" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2365419705" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2365419705?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2365419705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5322286759989577699">2.5 Stars. Unfortunately, I did not love this book and it is probably my least favorite of Gillian Flynn's work. As this was her debut, I'm happy to say I feel her later works show great improvement and a lot of strength.<br/><br/>CW: self-harm, sexualization of children, murder, child abuse (I don't normally put content warnings under spoilers but this warning is so integral to the ending AND it's so specific that I don't want people attacking me for spoiling the book) <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Munchausen By Proxy </span></span>
  <span id="freeText5322286759989577699" style="display:none">2.5 Stars. Unfortunately, I did not love this book and it is probably my least favorite of Gillian Flynn's work. As this was her debut, I'm happy to say I feel her later works show great improvement and a lot of strength.<br /><br />CW: self-harm, sexualization of children, murder, child abuse (I don't normally put content warnings under spoilers but this warning is so integral to the ending AND it's so specific that I don't want people attacking me for spoiling the book) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Munchausen By Proxy <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />I think Gillian Flynn is a brilliant writer, but it was quite obvious that <i>Sharp Objects</i> was her debut. Her prose remains easy to engage with, but it is much more simplistic compared to her later works. That being said, the writing was one of the elements I actually appreciated in this story.<br /><br />I didn't particularly love the plot of the story. The idea of children being murdered and a journalist having to return to their small hometown was super intriguing to me, but the execution fell flat in my opinion. The "darkness" I constantly see associated with this book is definitely present - this book is not for the faint of heart, but truthfully, the story was boring in my opinion. I understand some people love small-town stories that focus on gossip and rumors, but it's not my cup of tea. I was missing the exhilarating plot twists from <i>Gone Girl</i> and <i>Dark Places</i>. It was very slow and for the most part, anticlimactic to me. I felt there were so many opportunities for more enticing, eventful scenes to be included but it was taken over by bland character interactions.<br /><br />The big reveals/plot twists are difficult to discuss because my experience is an amalgamation of "This is surprising" and "This is expected." I feel the best way to describe it is I felt the resolution of the story was clever and well constructed, but it was partially anticipated. I feel the minute details surrounding the resolution were stronger than the big reveal itself if that makes sense. <br /><br />Additionally, the ending felt very rushed as the truth of the mystery is revealed through Camille recollecting the events instead of being shown actively through the story. I think it would have been much stronger had we followed the revaluation in real-time along with Camille's initial reactions as opposed to having the events relayed to readers at a later time. Again, I feel this is a marker of this novel being Flynn's debut work and I can confirm that there is little "telling, not showing" in her future books. <br /><br />Overall, I wasn't a fan of <i>Sharp Objects</i>, I think it just wasn't for me, but I'll continue to love Gillian Flynn's work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5322286759989577699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3190746155" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3190746155" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77602709-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519184646p2/77602709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3190746155?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/77602709-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/49761893-sharp-objects">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3190746155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9247984158521188479"><b>3.4</b>/5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/><br/><blockquote>“The face you give the world tells the world how to treat you.” </blockquote><br/><br/>Wow well this was... disturbing. <b>And sick and twisted and depraved and degenerate. </b>Possibly incest. I liked it! But didn't love it. Prior to reading this book, I had watched the mini series from HBO. And then naturally, I bought the book and didn't read it until now. Yes, the series came out 2 years ago and I'm reading the book in 2020, shut up. But let's talk about it.<br/><br/>Camille was a very interesting protagonist to </span>
  <span id="freeText9247984158521188479" style="display:none"><b>3.4</b>/5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br /><blockquote>“The face you give the world tells the world how to treat you.” </blockquote><br /><br />Wow well this was... disturbing. <b>And sick and twisted and depraved and degenerate. </b>Possibly incest. I liked it! But didn't love it. Prior to reading this book, I had watched the mini series from HBO. And then naturally, I bought the book and didn't read it until now. Yes, the series came out 2 years ago and I'm reading the book in 2020, shut up. But let's talk about it.<br /><br />Camille was a very interesting protagonist to read about. <b>She has a very dark past, a disturbed family, history of violence, abuse and self harm</b> and now after years of not being back to her hometown and having being "saved" so to speak, she ends up back in the rabbit hole. Which brings back many bad memories, awkward meetings with old classmates, gossip, and most importantly... a reunion with her toxic mother. I didn't like Camille as a person. She was very unlikable and snobbish to me. But I liked reading about her and delving more into her psyche. Finally a good "unlikable characters" book.<br /><br />The storyline was pretty basic, two little girls are killed in a small town... reporter has to go there and write an article about it... but in this case the reporter is from the town. <b>This fucking town man!</b> Is this how people are like in small towns in America? Like honestly, 13 years olds acting like 18 years olds? What the fuck was that about? They could just up the ages a tiny bit... 15 would have been more realistic. Looking like that and acting like that at 13 does not happen often. Maybe they could have done this with Amma only, which yes was the most popular and mean girl in school blah blah blah, but the other girls don't really fall much behind. They are in middle school for God's sake! No. Couldn't buy it. Tell me please, if 13 year olds in America act like this, I truly want to know.<br /><br />The mystery was thrilling but at times it fell flat. There are moments were the plot was backtracking I could say? I can't really explain it but I guess I could say some things felt very repetitive sometimes. Conversations and characters mostly. Also thoughts in Camille's mind and the way she expressed them. Maybe this book could be smaller and it would be more impactful and fast paced.<br /><br />One of my biggest problems with this book was the ending and the "twist". The revelation was written in such a weird way that I literally had to go back to my audiobook and book (yes I listen to audiobooks at 2.3 while reading the book too to read faster, trust me it works, especially if you're bilingual) to understand what the fuck just happened. Luckily, I didn't remember the twist from the mini series and when I remembered it I got that "OH SHIT HOW DID I FORGET THIS" but the presentation could have been better. <b>It was a good plot twist buried by the writing and presentation.</b><br /><br />To sum up, this was a good but not great mystery thriller for me. If you enjoy mystery thrillers that depend mostly on abusive relationships and character studies, you will like this a lot more. If you want good world building and a nice plot twist, you won't like it extremely much. And before I go... <b>FUCK THE MOTHER.</b> K bye!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9247984158521188479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_414100373" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/414100373" />
    <a title="Will Byrnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes"><img alt="Will Byrnes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291462190p2/1526851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/414100373?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will Byrnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will Byrnes" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes">Will Byrnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780307341549" href="/book/show/66559.Sharp_Objects">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer414100373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6710686857903223783">Camille Preaker is a young Chicago reporter with a troubled past. When a second young girl goes missing in her home town, Wind Gap, MO, Camille’s fatherly boss sends her down to get the inside scoop. Who says you can’t go home again? Well, maybe you can, but would you really want to? There is a reason she is in Chicago, instead of Podunk, MO, and the danger for Camille lies as much with her delicate psychological state, a product of her childhood, as it might with a psycho-killer on the loose. "</span>
  <span id="freeText6710686857903223783" style="display:none">Camille Preaker is a young Chicago reporter with a troubled past. When a second young girl goes missing in her home town, Wind Gap, MO, Camille’s fatherly boss sends her down to get the inside scoop. Who says you can’t go home again? Well, maybe you can, but would you really want to? There is a reason she is in Chicago, instead of Podunk, MO, and the danger for Camille lies as much with her delicate psychological state, a product of her childhood, as it might with a psycho-killer on the loose. "Qu'est-ce que c'est ?" <br><br>Wind Gap is home to an array of characters left over from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GCB_(TV_series)" rel="nofollow noopener">GCB</a>, (Yes, I know it was published before the show) Stepford and Village of the Damned, and mix in a bit of Mommie Dearest and Cruella de Vil. Sounds like fun, no? Sorry to disappoint, but not so much. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506658406i/24037919.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Gillian Flynn</b> - Image from Orion Books<br><br>Less than a year ago a young girl was found dead, floating in a stream, strangled, with her teeth removed. Now a second girl, about the same age, has gone missing and folks are fearing the worst. Well, duh-uh. ‘Ere long the body is found wedged in a foot-wide space between two buildings, sans pearly whites. The game is afoot.<br><br>Camille has to cope with an uncooperative local Sheriff and then try to get some, any information from the very cute Kansas City detective who had been brought in to help out. Camille is presented as a dish, and there is definite sexual tension between the reporter and the town’s visiting investigator. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ok I really first wrote “between the reporter and the town’s visiting dick”, but my wife (who does not have the mind of a 12 year old boy) shamed me into removing it. Usually she does not see my material until it is on line but had expressed curiosity about the book, so got a preview.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1530851096i/25930452._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Amy Adams as Camille Preaker – image from NY Times<br><br>Camille makes the rounds, visiting the families of the victims, reconnecting, for good or ill with her former schoolmates, most of whom seem never to have heard of the women’s movement. But the largest connection for Camille in Wind Gap is her childhood home, inhabited by her mother, stepfather and half-sister. Cue thunder and lightning, creepy music and under the chin lighting. Mom, ironically named Adora, has the warm presence of a guillotine and Camille’s stepfather, Alan, appearing in various costumes, seems to need only a pinky ring and fluffy white lap cat to complete the cartoon. <br><br>We all know what happens when we return to the houses in which we were raised. We regress. Come on, admit it. We behave like the children we once were. At the very least we feel the tug of those urges. In Camille’s case, her home life was, shall we say, lacking. Her little sister, Marian, had died when Camille was kid. Attempting to cope with that and some other issues, she took to a bit of long-lasting self-destructive behavior. In case the razor on the cover of this book is not obvious enough, Camille is a cutter, or was anyway. Not just lines, but words. And the words on her skin pop into her mind as she digs into her research and takes on the psychological challenges of her home town. We learn early on that she had spent some time in rehab attempting to overcome her addiction. The Camille we meet here may be scarred, but is trying to carve a less destructive path forward for herself. It is a challenge, and represents a parallel set of mysteries. How did the adolescent Camille reach a place where she felt it necessary to indulge in such harmful behavior? What’s the deal with her family? Camille has to figure out not only the secret of the two murders, but her own history.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1530851096i/25930453._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Eliza Scanlen as Amma Crellin<br><br>Her background makes it easier for her to relate to her thirteen-year-old stepsister, Amma, who knew both the dead girls. They share some traits. Like Camille as a kid, Amma (a word that usually means “mother”) is a mean-girl group leader, headstrong, bright, and not someone you would ever cross. Amma is physically precocious, and behaviorally far beyond that. She can usually be seen with her girl-pack, laughing at funerals, or, metaphorically, kicking cripples. <br><br>Adding to the creepshow atmosphere, and keeping the cutting notion sharp, there is a slaughterhouse in town. One particular scene resonated a lot. In the slaughterhouse, sows are positioned on their sides, with absolutely no room to maneuver, and piglets are brought to the captive females to nurse. It is not an inducement to eating bacon. It so happened that I had seen a film, <i>Samsara</i>, the day before reading the book, in which this very scene was shown. In the book, an added element is that a young girl sits and watches this with unnatural pleasure.<br><br>We learn more about the victims in time, and it is a somewhat fun ride. But every now and then Camille does or says something that makes you shake your jowls like Louis Black approaching a punch line and burble out a WTF? And those moments take one out of the story.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1530851096i/25930454._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Patricia Clarkson as Adora Crellin<br><br>There is clear evidence of talent on display. I liked the prefiguring of the opening in which Preaker is looking at her latest story, about a crack-addled mother who abandoned her kids. Mothering figures prominently in the story. Using a slaughterhouse to echo the cutting Camille practices on herself, and maybe some other horrors as well, may have been a bit heavy-handed, but fine, ok. Having Camille carve words into her skin definitely seems over the top to me, a bit of literary license, but fine, ok. I enjoyed the fun noir twang with which Flynn begins her story, but it seemed to fade quite a lot over the course of 254 pages. Fine, ok. And for fun, Camille, who has been known to hoist a few, manages to visit what seems every bar in town. I took it to be a running joke, but I am not 100% certain. Fine, ok. I felt a lot of fine, ok here. <br><br>There is some sex, a fair bit of sexiness, some serious creepiness, a bit of satisfaction to be had in the procedural elements of finding this out then that. But while there may have been satiric intent at work, the characters were either too inconsistent, too thinly drawn or even cartoonish to invest much emotionally. <i>Sharp Objects</i> may have been the bleeding edge of Flynn’s career as a novelist, and it is not a bad first cut, but it left me hoping that she would apply her obvious talent with finer lines next time, maybe use some subtler shades and etch more believable characters, give us material we could dig into a little deeper. <br><br><br>The images (except for the author’s) are from the HBO mini-series made from the book.<br><br>=============================<b>EXTRA STUFF</b><br><br>Links to the author’s <a href="http://gillian-flynn.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">personal</a>, <a href="https://twitter.com/thegillianflynn?lang=en" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> and <a href="https://www.facebook.com/authorgillianflynn" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">FB</a> pages<br><br>March 23, 2013 - GR pal <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/105244-peg" rel="nofollow noopener">Peg</a> clued us in to a <a href="https://medium.com/@Powells/i-was-not-a-nice-little-girl-c2df01e0ae1" rel="nofollow noopener">wonderful piece</a> Flynn wrote for Powell's, that goes a way to illuminating her literary choices. If you read this or other books by Flynn, this short piece is MUST READ material. <br>BTW, Powell's moved the location of this file. Thanks to sharp-eyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8530205-marty-fried" rel="nofollow noopener">Marty Fried</a>, it is linked again.<br><br>NY Times - <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2018/11/08/magazine/gillian-flynn-women.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Gillian Flynn Peers Into the Dark Side of Femininity</a> - by Lauren Oyler - Nov. 8, 2018<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6710686857903223783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_102141639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102141639" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102141639?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780307341549" href="/book/show/66559.Sharp_Objects">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of all things disturbing</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      Rachel Michaux
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=only-i-will-like">only-i-will-like</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=mysteries-thrillers-horror">mysteries-thrillers-horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102141639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9157944935694032721"><b>Update 10/2018</b><br/>Doesn't seem that edgy 8 years later. We are not lacking in female anti-heroes now. The novel and the show complement each other rather well. Liked the neater ending of the book more though, but the show is a visual feast. Interesting how the show creators chickened out and made Amma older, to not offend our sensibilities? Amy Adams is fantastic as Camille.<br/><br/><b>Original review</b><br/>If you ask me which words come into my mind first whenever I think of this book, my answer will be: <i>nasty</i>, <i>dark</i>,</span>
  <span id="freeText9157944935694032721" style="display:none"><b>Update 10/2018</b><br />Doesn't seem that edgy 8 years later. We are not lacking in female anti-heroes now. The novel and the show complement each other rather well. Liked the neater ending of the book more though, but the show is a visual feast. Interesting how the show creators chickened out and made Amma older, to not offend our sensibilities? Amy Adams is fantastic as Camille.<br /><br /><b>Original review</b><br />If you ask me which words come into my mind first whenever I think of this book, my answer will be: <i>nasty</i>, <i>dark</i>, <i>twisted</i>, <i>disturbing</i>.<br /><br />In this rather traumatizing psychological thriller Camille Preaker, a troubled newspaper reporter, is sent to her home town to get the inside scoop on the murders of two preteen girls - both were strangled and had their teeth removed. As we follow Camille on her quest to obtain as much information as possible about the crimes, we learn much more than we bargained for. The small town of Wind Gap, in the fashion of Twin Peaks, is filled to the brim with dark secrets, and not the least of them is the twisted dynamics in Camille's own family...<br /><br />For me the most remarkable aspect of this book is that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2383.Gillian_Flynn" title="Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gillian Flynn</a> succeeds in creating a novel main characters of which are nasty women. I am so used to books where women are victims and all evil is committed by bad, bad men. Not so in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1343441.Sharp_Objects" title="Sharp Objects by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Sharp Objects</a>. Women of Wind Gap are both victims and perpetrators, they are promiscuous and abusive, self-destructive and violent. Men are only fixtures in their lives and pawns in their sick games. If anything, this is a refreshing twist on the old tired genre of murder mystery. <br /><br />I liked the psychological aspect of this novel as well. Flynn skillfully portrays how differently people react to the abuse in their lives - some direct the pain onto themselves, some inflict it on others - and both ways are equally damaging to one's psyche.<br /><br />I definitely wouldn't recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1343441.Sharp_Objects" title="Sharp Objects by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Sharp Objects</a> to squeamish. There is a lot of disturbing stuff in this book - promiscuous young girls, self-mutilation, sexual abuse, drugs. This is not a comfort read by any means. However I found it fascinating (in a I-can't-stop-watching-this-train-wreck way) and hard to put down. I will certainly read Flynn's other novel - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5886881.Dark_Places" title="Dark Places by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Places</a>. Well, as soon as I psychologically recover from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1343441.Sharp_Objects" title="Sharp Objects by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Sharp Objects</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9157944935694032721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1787040658" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1787040658" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1787040658?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=mystery-and-thriller">mystery-and-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t">finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1787040658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17178044723562461842"><b>1 Star<br/><br/>Overview:</b> <br/><br/>I should have known better. I don’t have an excuse.<br/><br/>I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2383.Gillian_Flynn' title='Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gillian Flynn</a>'s other book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl' title='Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Gone Girl</a>, last year—and wasn’t a fan. Everyone raved about it, but I found the characters shallow, the plot twists weak, and the narrative so busy being cynical it didn’t seem to know what it was trying to say. <br/><br/>Nevertheless, I’d heard <i>great</i> things about Gillian Flynn’s writing. So I went into this with an open mind--- maybe I had just started with the wrong book! <br/><br/>But I <i>really should have known </i></span>
  <span id="freeText17178044723562461842" style="display:none"><b>1 Star<br /><br />Overview:</b> <br /><br />I should have known better. I don’t have an excuse.<br /><br />I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2383.Gillian_Flynn" title="Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gillian Flynn</a>'s other book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a>, last year—and wasn’t a fan. Everyone raved about it, but I found the characters shallow, the plot twists weak, and the narrative so busy being cynical it didn’t seem to know what it was trying to say. <br /><br />Nevertheless, I’d heard <i>great</i> things about Gillian Flynn’s writing. So I went into this with an open mind--- maybe I had just started with the wrong book! <br /><br />But I <i>really should have known better. </i> When I wanted to DNF this around 13% of the way through, I should have trusted my instincts and realized Flynn's writing just isn't for me. But I kept seeing reviews talking about “the twist” and how the ending was the best part. So I persevered. Safe to say, I didn’t like this. Actually I think I disliked it more than Gone Girl. <br /><br /><i>*language and mature themes ahead, due to the nature of this book* </i><br /><br /><b>Pros:</b><br /><br /> I don’t like to rate things so low. I really don’t, and I rarely do it. I was initially going to round this up to a two-star, but I realized I didn't have a real reason. I have 'criteria' for all my ratings and in order to earn two-stars from me, a book has to contain <i>some</i> elements I liked. This contained a handful of descriptions I liked. <i>That’s it.</i> <br /><br />At points in the text, Flynn compares a new-found murder victim’s appearance to that of a baby doll, with mouth open and ready to suckle. This was an incredibly creepy simile that I thought painted the scene quite clearly. <br /><br />Then later, Flynn describes a woman as having “hips like antlers.” In regards to the bony prominence that juts out against the rest of the woman's body. Again, I thought this was an incredibly inventive description that also perfectly illustrated the character.<br /><br /> <b>Cons:</b> <br /><br />Oh boy. Here we go. <br /><br />What were these characters supposed to be? Every single character was filled with an intense hatred and cynicism about everything. They were all incredibly violent, shallow people <i>with no other defining characteristics</i> They were all very boring, flat people who just seemed to be awful without any motivation. <br /><br />It seems Flynn’s work relies upon a belief that all people are inherently evil and selfish—which is a popular theory in itself that I’ve seen in a wide variety of fiction. <i>But the characters still need to make sense. </i> <br /><br />Everything was needlessly dark? Like I just don’t understand?<br /><br />I don’t have a problem with darker books. I think a story can be just as dark and twisted as the author feels it needs to be, as long as it still tells the story <i>well</i> This just seemed to include random gritty details or supppppeeerrr intense descriptions. The main character’s struggle with mental health problems and self-harm (is this a spoiler? It’s pretty evident from the book’s blurb) was never discussed in any sort of nuanced way. Instead, it’s used almost as a plot device to show just how “edgy” this book is. <br /><br />I don’t mind profanity or adult material in adult books. But the over-abundance of it in this book, again, just seemed like it was trying to hard to be gritty or “edgy.” Everything was needlessly sexualized even when the conversations or characters didn’t call for it at that time. <br /><br />This book was too short to be <i>so boring</i> The pace was irrationally languid despite the intense subject matter, and it felt like it took chapters and chapters for the characters to stop just discussing things and for things to actually happen. <br /><br />There’s been a fairly large amount of controversy surrounding the way Gillian Flynn, a self-proclaimed feminist, writes her female characters.<br /><br />You have those who think it’s problematic all of her female characters are such awful people: Like <a href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/nile-cappello/how-gone-girl-is-misogynistic_b_5572288.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Huffington Post</a><a href="http://www.vulture.com/2014/10/yes-gone-girl-has-a-woman-problem.html" rel="nofollow noopener"> and</a><a href="http://the-artifice.com/gillian-flynn-women-mystery-novels/" rel="nofollow noopener"> others.</a><br /><br />And then you have those who believe <i>all</i> her characters are horrible people, and that feminism means allowing for female villains and anti-heroes: <a href="https://mic.com/articles/100664/no-gone-girl-does-not-have-a-woman-problem#.wj3O3fnIM" rel="nofollow noopener"> Including</a><a href="https://www.theguardian.com/books/2013/may/01/gillian-flynn-bestseller-gone-girl-misogyny " rel="nofollow noopener"> Flynn herself. </a> <br /><br />I won’t be touching upon this controversy too much, as I don’t think there’s very much I can say that hasn’t already been discussed. I personally want female villains and anti-heroes who are just as complex as their male counter parts—which I didn’t find in this book where <i>all</i> the characters were so shallow. <br /><br />There were a few things that <i>did</i> seem problematic:<br /><br />-	The main character calls a man a “sexist, liberal lefty practicing sexual discrimination” for believing a drunk woman having sex with an entire football team without her explicit consent was sexual assault. Even when when it was revealed the woman was a minor. <br /><br />-	This entire quote: <i> “Sometimes I think illness sits inside every woman, waiting for the right moment to bloom. I have known so many sick women all my life. Women with chronic pain, with ever-gestating diseases. Women with conditions. Men, sure, they have bone snaps, they have backaches, they have a surgery or two, yank out a tonsil, insert a shiny plastic hip.” </i> <br /><br />-	The whole book is filled with the assumption that woman are either so fragile they are sick and broken all the time, or that they just love the attention of being sick. I understand a large part of this was related to the situations Camille was raised in and her mother, but it extended to every other character as well. <br /><br />-	<i>“Women get consumed. Not surprising, considering the sheer amount of traffic a woman's body experiences. Tampons and speculums. Cocks, fingers, vibrators and more, between the legs, from behind, in the mouth.” </i> WOMEN ARE NOT COMMODITIES THAT GET CONSUMED. The implication that a woman can be ‘run-down’ based off the amount of things she’s had in her orifices is completely disgusting.<br /><br />I guessed whodunit less than halfway through. The reasoning was interesting, though the way it was all revealed match the same odd, explicit tone as the rest of the story. <br /><br /><b> In Conclusion: </b><br /><br /> Safe to say, I will <i>not</i> be reading Dark Places.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17178044723562461842" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2015021250" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2015021250" />
    <a title="j e w e l s" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s"><img alt="j e w e l s" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552606306p2/68216634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2015021250?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="j e w e l s" class="user" itemprop="url" name="j e w e l s" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s">j e w e l s</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=twister-hall-of-fame">twister-hall-of-fame</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=books-bejeweled">books-bejeweled</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2015021250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11469613209935711295"><i>“I just think some women aren't made to be mothers. And some women aren't made to be daughters.” </i><br/>― Gillian Flynn, Sharp Objects<br/><br/>This is one of the darkest, most disturbing books I've ever read. And I love it. Well, today I love it. I picked it up years ago, started reading and was like "no way Jose". I had read Dark Places and Gone Girl and, of course, thought I could handle Sharp Objects, the Gillian Flynn debut. I wasn't ready at the time for this <b>little monster of a book.</b><br/><br/>The extremely creepy p</span>
  <span id="freeText11469613209935711295" style="display:none"><i>“I just think some women aren't made to be mothers. And some women aren't made to be daughters.” </i><br />― Gillian Flynn, Sharp Objects<br /><br />This is one of the darkest, most disturbing books I've ever read. And I love it. Well, today I love it. I picked it up years ago, started reading and was like "no way Jose". I had read Dark Places and Gone Girl and, of course, thought I could handle Sharp Objects, the Gillian Flynn debut. I wasn't ready at the time for this <b>little monster of a book.</b><br /><br />The extremely creepy plot revolves around a serial killer in a Missouri town, and the reporter who has returned from Chicago to cover the event. Just a few of the themes include dysfunctional families, violence and self-harm. But there is so much more.<br /><br />As I've mentioned before, I've read a lot of blasé, boring domestic noir lately. Give me a book with some meat on its bones! Blake Crouch's Dark Matter got my motor running again and I just couldn't go back to some of those wimpily <i>-made up word</i> written mysteries.<br /><br />If you're caught in a summer stagnation, wake yourself up with this book. It's probably lying on a shelf in your house somewhere. Just prepare yourself. Flynn is an expert "description writer" and some of the things she describes are not pretty. At all. As in sick, sick, sick. <br /><br />Yes, the characters are seriously f****d up! I don't need my heroine to be shiny and pristine. Every person in this story has got issues.  Who knows what kind of childhood some people endure? Aren't you curious as to WHY they are weird? I always am!<br /><br />I know some readers are all, "but, I don't really like the characters, I can't root for anyone..." Ok, then this book isn't for you. But, I'm telling you, Gillian Flynn is a master at blueprinting the human psyche into a living breathing character that you won't soon, if ever, forget. You'll probably even have a nightmare or two, after all, Stephen King is a huge Flynn fan.</span>

<div id="review_663470928" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/663470928" />
    <a title="Paquita Maria Sanchez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2508169-paquita-maria-sanchez"><img alt="Paquita Maria Sanchez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594814608p2/2508169.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/663470928?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paquita Maria Sanchez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paquita Maria Sanchez" href="/user/show/2508169-paquita-maria-sanchez">Paquita Maria Sanchez</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780307341549" href="/book/show/66559.Sharp_Objects">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2508169-paquita-maria-sanchez?shelf=literature">literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer663470928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5353323435304014529">Well, this was a pleasant surprise. I remember all the ruckus over Gillian Flynn a while back, and my resulting tracing (<i>not</i> carving) of a mental note on my palm that I should eventually read something by this gal because everybody was all in a tizzy over her wonderfulmousnessity back whenever, and I was confused by that fact based on the book descriptions alone. It all just sounded like mass market thrillers dressed up in fancy lit fic suits. Ya know, the stuff of mediocre books which sometimes</span>
  <span id="freeText5353323435304014529" style="display:none">Well, this was a pleasant surprise. I remember all the ruckus over Gillian Flynn a while back, and my resulting tracing (<i>not</i> carving) of a mental note on my palm that I should eventually read something by this gal because everybody was all in a tizzy over her wonderfulmousnessity back whenever, and I was confused by that fact based on the book descriptions alone. It all just sounded like mass market thrillers dressed up in fancy lit fic suits. Ya know, the stuff of mediocre books which sometimes get passed to great directors, screen-writers, and actors, and then maybe turned into really good movies. Basically, I just wanted to understand what the hell was going on with this new girl at the middle school who showed up mid-semester and got all the attention just because her folks were always out of town so you could smoke pot at her house and raid the liquor cabinet or whatever. I shamefully admit, I was ready and willing to dislike her. Maybe I'm shallow, and so was put off by the pop of it all. Maybe that one time I saw <i>Gone Girl</i> as a stickered best-selling! 20% off Audio Book, I silently simmered further, my eyes squintier still. Whatever, it doesn't matter. I was wrong. I frequently forget that this is a very frequent occurrence. <br /><br />From the first couple of pages, maybe even the first, I acknowledged my ass-umptions. The writing is astute in its observations, visceral in its descriptions. And the narrator is all messed up, which hear, hear. I actually stopped when I realized I'd read about 100 pages without looking away, and thought to myself: I should read more thrillers, huh? Well, no. Most of them that I have come across are not this confidently, this surgically composed. There is no fluffy stuffing here, just good, straight storytelling with the added bonus of cautiously crafted prose. Also, it's really fucking creepy, and me being creeped out by anything at this point in my life is a pretty tall order. I mean, aside from spiders and needles and being buried alive and over-sexualized pre-teen Lolita-types who collect and dress like that Bratz line of toy dolls. Now <i>that</i> shit is creepy. Fortunately, a couple of those things are directly addressed in this novel. My goodness, it must be terrifying having a daughter, or being an adult dude today. Or a human at all. Yeah, it is.<br /><br />The story itself meanders in a way which is icky, thoroughly hammered out, and fairly unpredictable. I may be inflating the rating because my expectations were so low, but that doesn't change the fact that I will be reading another novel by this author because she isn't some hack; she just likes to slum a little, subject-wise. And that's more than okay with me, it turns out. <br /><br />Cutters, Lolitas, Munchausen by Proxy, obsessions, family hatreds, drug abuse, scandalous sex, graphic violence, serial murder, wealth, poverty, popularity, bullying, hypochondria, crippling jealousy, police procedural bullshit, alcoholism, taboo masturbation fantasies, eating disorders, small town smothering, big city anonymity, career/life/love failures, falls from grace, the hell of being romantically idealized by someone and then seen in vivid, horrible detail for what you really are: all addressed in this slim little novel. It's pretty fucking good, to be honest. Just...don't loan it to your mother. And hope that no one in this novel reminds you of your mother. Don't be bothered if you see a little of yourself here and there, though. We're all headcases sometimes, right? Please just agree with me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5353323435304014529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review663470928">

<div id="review_2731853201" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2731853201" />
    <a title="The Burning Rose (Jess)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess"><img alt="The Burning Rose (Jess)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605317941p2/48477217.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2731853201?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Burning Rose (Jess)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Burning Rose (Jess)" href="/user/show/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess">The Burning Rose (Jess)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780307341549" href="/book/show/66559.Sharp_Objects">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2731853201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17056270543904972659">3/5 stars.<br/>The book tells of a young reporter named Camille. She escaped from the town where she grew up years ago to break away from the cruel life she lived, and to start a new life.<br/>Years later, Camille had to return to the town for the article she needed to publish. Camille, who did everything to disavow this town, found herself returning there unwillingly.<br/><br/>I know that in the description of the book, it says it's a murder story. But I wouldn't describe this book that way.<br/>True, there were brutal</span>
  <span id="freeText17056270543904972659" style="display:none">3/5 stars.<br />The book tells of a young reporter named Camille. She escaped from the town where she grew up years ago to break away from the cruel life she lived, and to start a new life.<br />Years later, Camille had to return to the town for the article she needed to publish. Camille, who did everything to disavow this town, found herself returning there unwillingly.<br /><br />I know that in the description of the book, it says it's a murder story. But I wouldn't describe this book that way.<br />True, there were brutal homicides in the town. True, the main character, Camille, is trying to figure out the murder. True, there are detectives, there are investigations. But after all, I wouldn't say the book is about the homicides.<br /><br />The book is about the main character. Her past and present. The book is about this strange and cruel town. The book is surrounding around Camille herself, her family and the town itself.<br /><br />I personally didn't like the book so much. It was... too dumb. Not the book itself tho, but the town. I hate this town. I'm not sure how to explain it, but while reading the book I just... felt bad. Just like that. I had a bad and restless feeling. This town, the people who live in it, the way they live. They are godless. They are cruel. They are hypocrites and liars. It's just so fucking dumb. If I lived there, I probably would’ve committed suicide. And I'm not kidding.<br /><br />And Camille, so broken on the inside, so twisted, so scarred, literally. She was scarred from the moment she was born in this town. But that's exactly the problem - everyone's scarred because of this town.<br /><br />I'm not sure how many stars I really want to give this book. After all, it was pretty interesting. But like I said, this book made me feel so bad. And even after I finished the book - the bad feeling remained there and gave me no rest. The ending was over well, but I personally didn’t feel rested, the book continued to disturb me even after I finished reading it. <br /><br />The only reason this book gets 3 stars and not less, is thanks to Flynn's writing. She writes incredibly, and she deserves a hundred stars just for her writing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17056270543904972659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
